<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the island in Antarctica. For the island in Washington State, see <a href="/wiki/Deception_Pass" title="Deception Pass">Deception Pass</a>. For the island in Chile, see <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_Chile#Deceit" title="List of islands of Chile">List of islands of Chile §&#160;Deceit</a>.</div>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deception_Island_Map.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Deception_Island_Map.svg/220px-Deception_Island_Map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Deception_Island_Map.svg/330px-Deception_Island_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Deception_Island_Map.svg/440px-Deception_Island_Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="820" data-file-height="763" /></a><figcaption>Deception Island map with the topography and the location of the stations and protected zones</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Deception Island</b> is in the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetland_Islands" title="South Shetland Islands">South Shetland Islands</a> close to the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Peninsula" title="Antarctic Peninsula">Antarctic Peninsula</a> with a large and usually "safe" natural harbor, which is occasionally affected by the underlying active volcano.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (July 2020)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> This island is the <a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">caldera</a> of an active <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, which seriously damaged local scientific stations in 1967 and 1969. The island previously held a whaling station. It is now a tourist destination with over 15,000 visitors per year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Two research stations are operated by Argentina and Spain during the summer season.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> While various countries have asserted sovereignty, it is still administered under the <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Treaty_System" title="Antarctic Treaty System">Antarctic Treaty System</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg/220px-20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg/330px-20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg/440px-20200101_105347_Telefon_Bay_Espen_Mills.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152" /></a><figcaption>Telefon Bay</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_(WSW).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg/220px-South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg/330px-South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg/440px-South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Caldera_wall_reflection_%28WSW%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="8688" data-file-height="5792" /></a><figcaption>Looking WSW from the center of the caldera</figcaption></figure>
<p>Located within the <a href="/wiki/Bransfield_Strait" title="Bransfield Strait">Bransfield Strait</a>, the island is roughly circular and horseshoe-shaped, with a maximum diameter around 15&#160;km (9.3&#160;mi). The highest peak, Mount Pond on the east side of the island, has an elevation of 539&#160;m (1,768&#160;ft), while Mount Kirkwood on the west has an elevation of 452&#160;m (1,483&#160;ft). Over half (57%) of the island is covered by <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a> up to 10&#160;m thick, ice-cored <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">moraines</a>, or ice-covered <a href="/wiki/Pyroclast" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyroclast">pyroclasts</a>. The centre of the island has been flooded by the sea to form a large bay, now called <a href="/wiki/Port_Foster" title="Port Foster">Port Foster</a>, about 10&#160;km (6.2&#160;mi) long and 7&#160;km (4.3&#160;mi) wide. The bay has a narrow entrance, just 500&#160;m (1,640&#160;ft) wide, called <a href="/wiki/Neptune%27s_Bellows" title="Neptune&#39;s Bellows">Neptune's Bellows</a>. The port is a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_basin" title="Oceanic basin">basin</a> with a flat floor up to 170&#160;m (560&#160;ft) deep with several small submarine <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_cone" title="Volcanic cone">cones</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lava_dome" title="Lava dome">domes</a>.  The port is rimmed by a shallow <a href="/wiki/Coastal_shelf" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal shelf">coastal shelf</a> with sandy-<a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravelly</a> beaches. The outer coast of the island is characterized by 30–70&#160;m (98–230&#160;ft) cliffs of rock or ice.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Raven's Rock, a navigation hazard, lies 2.5&#160;m (8.2&#160;ft) below the water in the middle of the channel. Just inside Neptune's Bellows lies the cove <a href="/wiki/Whalers_Bay_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="Whalers Bay (South Shetland Islands)">Whalers Bay</a>, which is bordered by a large <a href="/wiki/Black_sand" title="Black sand">black sand</a> beach. Several <a href="/wiki/Maar" title="Maar">maars</a> line the inside rim of the caldera, with some containing <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_crater_lake" title="Volcanic crater lake">crater lakes</a> (including one named Crater Lake). Others form bays within the harbour, such as the 1&#160;km (0.6&#160;mi) wide Whalers Bay. Other features of the island include <a href="/wiki/Mount_Kirkwood" title="Mount Kirkwood">Mount Kirkwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fumarole_Bay" title="Fumarole Bay">Fumarole Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sewing-Machine_Needles" title="Sewing-Machine Needles">Sewing-Machine Needles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telefon_Bay" title="Telefon Bay">Telefon Bay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telefon_Ridge" title="Telefon Ridge">Telefon Ridge</a>.
</p><p>The linear <a href="/w/index.php?title=Costa_Recta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Costa Recta (page does not exist)">Costa Recta</a> spanning most of the east coast is hypothesised to be a scarp of a retreated submarine fault.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A 2016 study on <a href="/wiki/Ardley_Island" title="Ardley Island">Ardley Island</a>, 120&#160;km (75&#160;mi) to the northeast, examined lake guano sediments and studied penguin population dynamics over 7,000&#160;years. Three of five population growth phases were terminated by a sudden crash, due to volcanic eruptions from the active volcano of Deception Island.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
The history of volcanic eruptions is still under investigation, but several larger eruptions happened in the last 10,000&#160;years.<sup id="cite_ref-AntoniadesGiralt2018_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AntoniadesGiralt2018-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geology">Geology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg/220px-Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg/330px-Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg/440px-Deceptionisland_oli_201882_lrg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1397" data-file-height="1164" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Landsat_8" title="Landsat 8">Landsat 8</a> satellite photograph taken on 23 March 2018</figcaption></figure>
<p>Deception Island is the exposed portion of an active <a href="/wiki/Shield_volcano" title="Shield volcano">shield volcano</a> 30&#160;km in diameter. The island is associated with <a href="/wiki/Bransfield_Basin" title="Bransfield Basin">Bransfield Basin</a> <a href="/wiki/Seafloor_spreading" title="Seafloor spreading">seafloor spreading</a> that includes a volcanic ridge and <a href="/wiki/Seamount" title="Seamount">seamounts</a> dating back to the <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a>. Deception Island <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">volcanic ash</a> layers have been found on other South Shetland Islands, the Bransfield Strait, the Scotia Sea and in South Pole <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">ice cores</a>. <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_tremor" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic tremor">Volcanic tremors</a> are common, originating from depths less than 10&#160;km. Historical eruptions occurred in 1839–1842, 1967, 1969, and 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: iii">&#58;&#8202;iii&#8202;</span></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Stratigraphy" title="Stratigraphy">Stratigraphy</a> of the island is characterized by the pre-<a href="/wiki/Caldera" title="Caldera">caldera</a> Port Foster Group and the post-caldera Mount Pond Group, both within the Deception Island Volcanic Complex. The Port Foster Group's principal <a href="/wiki/Outcrop" title="Outcrop">outcrops</a> are located at South Point, Cathedral Crags near Entrance Point and north of Punta de la Descubierta forming spectacular coastal cliffs along the western portion of the island. The group is composed of the Fumarole Bay Formation consisting of <a href="/wiki/Hydrovolcanic_eruption" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydrovolcanic eruption">hydrovolcanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Tephra" title="Tephra">tephra</a>, the Basaltic Shield Formation consisting of <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lavas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strombolian_eruption" title="Strombolian eruption">Strombolian</a> <a href="/wiki/Scoria" title="Scoria">scoria</a>, and the Outer Coast <a href="/wiki/Tuff" title="Tuff">Tuff</a> <a href="/wiki/Formation_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Formation (geology)">Formation</a> consisting of <a href="/wiki/Lapilli" title="Lapilli">lapilli</a>-tuffs. The Mount Pond Group dominates the surface geology and consists of the <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_rock" title="Pyroclastic rock">pyroclastic</a> Baily Head and Pendulum Cove formations, both formed during hydrovolcanic eruptions, and the Stonethrow Ridge Formation consisting of tuff <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_cone" title="Volcanic cone">cone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maar" title="Maar">maar</a> deposits.  The caldera collapsed as either a hydrovolcanic eruption of the Outer Coast Tuff Formation, releasing about 30 <a href="/wiki/Cubic_kilometer" class="mw-redirect" title="Cubic kilometer">cubic kilometers</a> of <a href="/wiki/Magma" title="Magma">magma</a>, or passively due to regional <a href="/wiki/Tectonics" title="Tectonics">tectonics</a>, since the island is at the intersection of the Bransfield Strait <a href="/wiki/Rift" title="Rift">rift</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Orthogonal" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthogonal">orthogonal</a> <a href="/wiki/Hero_fracture_zone" title="Hero fracture zone">Hero fracture zone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie2_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie2-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smellie3_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie3-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deception-Island-Map.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Deception-Island-Map.jpg/220px-Deception-Island-Map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="349" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Deception-Island-Map.jpg/330px-Deception-Island-Map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Deception-Island-Map.jpg/440px-Deception-Island-Map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1302" data-file-height="2065" /></a><figcaption>1829 map</figcaption></figure>
<p>The first authenticated sighting of Deception Island was by the British sealers William Smith and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Bransfield" title="Edward Bransfield">Edward Bransfield</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Brig" title="Brig">brig</a> <i>Williams</i> in January&#160;1820. It was first visited and explored by the American sealer <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Palmer" title="Nathaniel Palmer">Nathaniel Palmer</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">sloop</a> <i>Hero</i> the following summer, on 15&#160;November 1820. He remained for two days, exploring the central bay.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Palmer named it "Deception Island" on account of its outward <a href="/wiki/Optical_illusion" title="Optical illusion">deceptive</a> appearance as a normal island, when the narrow entrance of <a href="/wiki/Neptune%27s_Bellows" title="Neptune&#39;s Bellows">Neptune's Bellows</a> revealed it rather to be a ring around a flooded caldera.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Palmer was part of an American sealing fleet from <a href="/wiki/Stonington,_Connecticut" title="Stonington, Connecticut">Stonington, Connecticut</a>, under the command of Benjamin Pendleton, consisting of 6&#160;ships. Port Fisher was used as their operational base from 1820 to 1821. Palmer met <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Gottlieb_von_Bellingshausen" title="Fabian Gottlieb von Bellingshausen">Bellingshausen</a> close to the island in Jan.&#160;1821, during the <a href="/wiki/First_Russian_Antarctic_Expedition" title="First Russian Antarctic Expedition">First Russian Antarctic Expedition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>A lighthouse named <b>Surgidero Iquique</b> was built on the island to guide vessels into <a href="/wiki/Deception_Station" title="Deception Station">Deception Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-listoflights111_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-listoflights111-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Whaling_and_sealing">Whaling and sealing</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Whaling and sealing"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Antarctic,_Deception_Island_(js)_43.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg/290px-Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="190" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg/435px-Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg/580px-Antarctic%2C_Deception_Island_%28js%29_43.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5603" data-file-height="3663" /></a><figcaption>Remains of the whaling station's <a href="/wiki/Cochran_boiler" class="mw-redirect" title="Cochran boiler">boilers</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Over the next few years, Deception became a focal point of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">fur-sealing</a> industry in the South Shetlands. The industry began with a handful of ships in the 1819–1820 summer season, rising to nearly a hundred in 1821–1822. While the island did not have a large seal population, it was a perfect natural harbour, mostly free from ice and winds, and a convenient rendezvous point. Some men likely lived ashore in tents or shacks for short periods during the summer, though no archaeological or documentary evidence survives to confirm this. Massive overhunting meant that the fur seals neared extinction in the South Shetlands within a few years, and the sealing industry collapsed as quickly as it had begun. Deception was abandoned again in approximately 1825.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Sealing captain Robert Fildes charted Port Foster in 1820–1821, which in 1829 became the first published Antarctica <a href="/wiki/Nautical_chart" title="Nautical chart">nautical chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1829, the British Naval Expedition to the South Atlantic under the command of <a href="/wiki/Henry_Foster_(scientist)" title="Henry Foster (scientist)">Captain Henry Foster</a> in <a href="/wiki/HMS_Chanticleer_(1808)" title="HMS Chanticleer (1808)">HMS&#160;<i>Chanticleer</i></a> stopped at Deception. The expedition conducted a topographic survey and scientific experiments, particularly pendulum and magnetic observations.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A watercolour made by Lieutenant Kendall of the <i>Chanticleer</i> during the visit may be the first image made of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A subsequent visit by the American elephant-sealer <i>Ohio</i> in 1842 reported the first recorded volcanic activity, with the southern shore "in flames".<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval,_Whalers_Bay,_Deception_Island.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg/290px-D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="252" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg/435px-D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg/580px-D%C3%B8rnberger_-_Flensing_av_bl%C3%A5hval%2C_Whalers_Bay%2C_Deception_Island.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1044" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Flensing" title="Flensing">Flensing</a> at <a href="/wiki/Whalers_Bay_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="Whalers Bay (South Shetland Islands)">Whalers Bay</a>, Deception Island. By 1912–1913, the island had 12&#160;factory ships, and 27&#160;catchers, occupying 200&#160;people, with 3,000&#160;rotting whale carcasses in the Whalers Bay area.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 4">&#58;&#8202;4&#8202;</span></sup></figcaption></figure>
<p>The second phase of human activity at Deception began in the early 20th&#160;century. In 1904, an active <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> industry was established at South Georgia, taking advantage of new technology and an almost untouched population of whales to make rapid profits. It spread south into the South Shetland Islands, where the lack of shore-based infrastructure meant that the whales had to be towed to moored <a href="/wiki/Factory_ship" title="Factory ship">factory ships</a> for processing; these needed a sheltered anchorage and a plentiful supply of fresh water, both of which could be found at Deception. In 1906, the <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norwegian</a>-<a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chilean</a> whaling company Sociedad Ballenera de Magallanes started using <a href="/wiki/Whalers_Bay_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="Whalers Bay (South Shetland Islands)">Whalers Bay</a> as a base for a single ship, the <i>Gobernador Bories</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Other whalers followed, with several hundred men resident at Deception during the Antarctic summers and as many as 13&#160;ships operating in peak years. In 1908, the British government formally declared the island to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands_Dependencies" title="Falkland Islands Dependencies">Falkland Islands Dependencies</a>, thus under British control, establishing postal services and appointing a magistrate and customs officer for the island. The magistrate was to ensure that whaling companies were paying appropriate licence fees to the Falklands government and ensuring adherence to catch quotas. A cemetery was built in 1908, a radio station in 1912, a hand-operated railway also in 1912,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and a small permanent magistrate's house in 1914.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
The cemetery, by far the largest in Antarctica, held graves for 35&#160;men along with a memorial to 10&#160;more presumed drowned.<sup id="cite_ref-Cm_7166_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cm_7166-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deception-Base.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deception-Base.jpg/290px-Deception-Base.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="190" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deception-Base.jpg/435px-Deception-Base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Deception-Base.jpg/580px-Deception-Base.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1260" data-file-height="825" /></a><figcaption>The destroyed British base</figcaption></figure>
<p>These were not the only constructions; as the factory ships of the period were only able to strip the blubber from whales and could not use the carcasses, <a href="/wiki/Hektor_Station" title="Hektor Station">a permanent on-shore station was established by the Norwegian company Hvalfangerselskabet Hektor A/S</a> in 1912 –  up to an estimated 40% of the available oil was being wasted by the ship-based system. This was the only successful shore-based industry ever to operate in Antarctica, reaping high profits in its first years.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A number of exploring expeditions visited Deception during these years, including the <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Wilkins" title="Hubert Wilkins">Wilkins-Hearst expedition</a> of 1928, when a <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Vega" title="Lockheed Vega">Lockheed Vega</a> was flown from a beach airstrip on the first successful flights in Antarctica.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The development of pelagic whaling in the 1920s, where factory ships fitted with a slipway could tow aboard entire whales for processing, meant that whaling companies were no longer tied to sheltered anchorages. A boom in pelagic Antarctic whaling followed, with companies now free to ignore quotas and escape the costs of licences. This rapidly led to overproduction of oil and a collapse in the market, and the less profitable and more heavily regulated shore-based companies had trouble competing. In early 1931, the Hektor factory finally ceased operation, ending commercial whaling at the island entirely.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Scientific_research">Scientific research</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Scientific research"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 16 November 1928, <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Wilkins" title="Hubert Wilkins">Hubert Wilkins</a> made the first Antarctic flight from a Whalers Bay ash runway.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Deception remained uninhabited for a decade, but was revisited in 1941 by the British auxiliary warship <a href="/wiki/SS_Queen_of_Bermuda" title="SS Queen of Bermuda">HMS <i>Queen of Bermuda</i></a>, which destroyed the oil tanks and some remaining supplies to ensure it could not be used as a German supply base.<sup id="cite_ref-Dibbern_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dibbern-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1942, an Argentine party aboard the <i>Primero de Mayo</i> visited and left signs and painted flags declaring the site Argentine territory; the following year, a British party with <a href="/wiki/MV_Carnarvon_Castle" title="MV Carnarvon Castle">HMS&#160;<i>Carnarvon Castle</i></a> returned to remove the signs.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1944, a British expedition under Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/James_Marr_(biologist)" title="James Marr (biologist)">James Marr</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> established a short-lived base on Deception Island as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tabarin" title="Operation Tabarin">Operation Tabarin</a>, which was carried out during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> to deny safe anchorages to enemy raiding vessels and to gather meteorological data for allied shipping in the South Atlantic. It also had the effect of strengthening British claims to the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Island_Dependencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Falkland Island Dependencies">Falkland Island Dependencies</a> that had begun being challenged<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> by <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>. Operation Tabarin would deny use of the area to the <i><a href="/wiki/Kriegsmarine" title="Kriegsmarine">Kriegsmarine</a></i>, which was known to use remote islands as rendezvous points, and address a fear that Japan might attempt to seize the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>. Following the end of the war, the research begun by Operation Tabarin continued in subsequent years, ultimately becoming the <a href="/wiki/British_Antarctic_Survey" title="British Antarctic Survey">British Antarctic Survey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In February 1953, as part of a post-war British effort to exert sovereignty over its claimed Antarctic territories, <a href="/wiki/HMS_Snipe_(U20)" title="HMS Snipe (U20)">HMS&#160;<i>Snipe</i>&#160;(U20)</a> landed a party of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a> on Deception Island to destroy an Argentinian and a Chilean military base; an action known as the <a href="/wiki/Deception_Island_incident" title="Deception Island incident">Deception Island incident</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 1961, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>'s president <a href="/wiki/Arturo_Frondizi" title="Arturo Frondizi">Arturo Frondizi</a> visited the island to show his country's interest. Regular visits were made by other countries operating in the Antarctic, including the 1964 visit of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard" title="United States Coast Guard">US Coast Guard</a> icebreaker <a href="/wiki/USCGC_Eastwind" title="USCGC Eastwind"><i>Eastwind</i></a>, which ran aground inside the harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>However, the volcano returned to activity in 1967 and 1969, destroying the existing scientific stations. Both British and Chilean stations were demolished, and the island was again abandoned for several years. The final major volcanic eruption was reported by the Russian Bellingshausen station on <a href="/wiki/King_George_Island_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="King George Island (South Shetland Islands)">King George Island</a> and the Chilean station Arturo Prat on <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Island" title="Greenwich Island">Greenwich Island</a>; both stations experienced major falls of ash on 13&#160;August 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuchs-1982_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuchs-1982-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page:  294">(p 294)</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Shetland-2016-Deception_Island%E2%80%93Deception_Station_(Argentine_base).jpg" title="File:South Shetland-2016-Deception Island–Deception Station (Argentine base).jpg"> </a></div>Argentine Base Decepción (2016)
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000, there were two summer-only scientific stations, the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_de_Castilla_Base" title="Gabriel de Castilla Base">Gabriel de Castilla Base</a><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and the Argentine <a href="/wiki/Decepci%C3%B3n_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Decepción Station">Decepción Station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ES27_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES27-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Remains of previous structures at Whalers Bay include rusting boilers and tanks, an <a href="/wiki/Hangar" title="Hangar">aircraft hangar</a>, and the British scientific station house (Biscoe House), with the middle torn out by the 1969 mudflows. A bright orange derelict airplane <a href="/wiki/Fuselage" title="Fuselage">fuselage</a>, which is that of a <a href="/wiki/De_Havilland_Canada_DHC-3_Otter" title="De Havilland Canada DHC-3 Otter">de Havilland Canada DHC-3 Otter</a> that belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>, was recovered in 2004. Plans to restore the airplane and return it to the island have been made.<sup id="cite_ref-ES27_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ES27-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deception-Hangar.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Deception-Hangar.jpg/220px-Deception-Hangar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Deception-Hangar.jpg/330px-Deception-Hangar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Deception-Hangar.jpg/440px-Deception-Hangar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1230" data-file-height="825" /></a><figcaption>The derelict hangar</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Russian cruise ship <a href="/wiki/MV_Lyubov_Orlova" title="MV Lyubov Orlova">MV&#160;<i>Lyubov Orlova</i></a> ran aground at Deception Island on 27&#160;November 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> She was towed off by the Spanish Navy <a href="/wiki/Icebreaker" title="Icebreaker">icebreaker</a> <i>Las Palmas</i> and made her own way to <a href="/wiki/Ushuaia" title="Ushuaia">Ushuaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tierra_del_Fuego" title="Tierra del Fuego">Tierra del Fuego</a>. She later became a <a href="/wiki/Ghost_ship" title="Ghost ship">ghost ship</a> in the North Atlantic after the towing line parted during an operation to scrap the vessel in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The first <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">commercial cruise ship</a> arrived in January&#160;1966.  By 1999, over 10,000&#160;tourists had visited the island.<sup id="cite_ref-smellie_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smellie-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 5">&#58;&#8202;5&#8202;</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Research_stations">Research stations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Research stations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Aguirre_Cerda">Aguirre Cerda</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Aguirre Cerda"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Aguirre_Cerda_Research_Station" title="Aguirre Cerda Research Station">President Pedro Aguirre Cerda Station</a> was a Chilean Antarctic base, located at <a href="/wiki/Pendulum_Cove" title="Pendulum Cove">Pendulum Cove</a> on Deception Island in the <a href="/wiki/South_Shetland_Islands" title="South Shetland Islands">South Shetland Islands</a>, inaugurated in 1955. It was evacuated in December 1967 when volcanic eruptions forced the evacuation of the base.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Deception">Deception</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Deception"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deception_Station" title="Deception Station">Deception Station</a> is an Argentine base located at Deception Island. The station was founded on 25 January 1948 and was a year-round station until December&#160;1967, when <a href="/wiki/Types_of_volcanic_eruptions" title="Types of volcanic eruptions">volcanic eruptions</a> forced the evacuation of the base. Since then, it has been inhabited only during the summer.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Gabriel_de_Castilla">Gabriel de Castilla</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Gabriel de Castilla"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg/220px-Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg/330px-Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg/440px-Gabriel-de-Castilla-Base.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a><figcaption>The Spanish <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_de_Castilla_Base" title="Gabriel de Castilla Base"><i>Gabriel de Castilla</i> Base</a></figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gabriel_de_Castilla_Base" title="Gabriel de Castilla Base">Gabriel de Castilla Base</a> is a Spanish research station located on Deception Island. The station was constructed in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Gutiérrez_Vargas_Refuge"><span id="Guti.C3.A9rrez_Vargas_Refuge"></span>Gutiérrez Vargas Refuge</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Gutiérrez Vargas Refuge"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The Gutiérrez Vargas Refuge, named after an aviation captain who died on 30 December 1955, was located at 1&#160;km (0.62&#160;mi) from Aguirre Cerda Station and was inaugurated on 12 February 1956. Its purpose was to serve as a refuge for the members of the station in case of fire. On 4 December 1967 the refuge was definitively abandoned, as was the Aguirre Cerda Station, due to a violent volcanic eruption. The remains of the refuge structure can still be seen on the beach where it was located.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Station_B">Station B</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Station B"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Antarctic research station</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1257001546"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1043192559">.mw-parser-output <p>In early 1944, a party of men from <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tabarin" title="Operation Tabarin">Operation Tabarin</a>, a British expedition, established a permanent scientific base named Station&#160;B.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This was occupied until 5&#160;December 1967, when an eruption forced a temporary withdrawal. It was used again between 4&#160;December 1968 and 23&#160;February 1969, when further volcanic activity caused it to be abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuchs-1982_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuchs-1982-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page:  291–292">(p 291–292)</span></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Environment">Environment</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Environment"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Deception-Tourists.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Deception-Tourists.jpg/290px-Deception-Tourists.jpg" decoding="async" width="290" height="194" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Deception-Tourists.jpg/435px-Deception-Tourists.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Deception-Tourists.jpg/580px-Deception-Tourists.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1205" data-file-height="806" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Hot_spring" title="Hot spring">Hot spring</a> at Port Foster, with the <i><a href="/wiki/MV_Explorer_(1969)" title="MV Explorer (1969)">MS Explorer</a></i> in the background</figcaption></figure>
<p>Deception Island has become a popular tourist stop in Antarctica because of its several colonies of <a href="/wiki/Chinstrap_penguin" title="Chinstrap penguin">chinstrap penguins</a>, as well as the possibility of making a warm bath by digging into the sands of the beach.
</p><p>After the Norwegian Coastal Cruise Liner <a href="/wiki/MS_Nordkapp" title="MS Nordkapp">MS&#160;<i>Nordkapp</i></a> ran aground off the coast of Deception Island on 30&#160;January 2007, fuel from the ship washed into a bay. Ecological damage has not yet been determined. On 4&#160;February 2007, the Spanish Gabriel de Castilla research station on Deception Island reported that water and sand tests were clean, and that they had not found signs of the oil, estimated as 500 to 750&#160;<a href="/wiki/Litre" title="Litre">L</a> of light diesel (130 to 200&#160;<a href="/wiki/US_gallon" class="mw-redirect" title="US gallon">US&#160;gal</a>; 110 to 160&#160;<a href="/wiki/Imperial_gallon" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial gallon">imp&#160;gal</a>).
</p><p>Deception Island exhibits some wildly varying <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a>. Near volcanic areas, the air can be as hot as 40&#160;°C (104&#160;°F), and water temperature can reach 70&#160;°C (158&#160;°F).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Antarctic_specially_protected_areas">Antarctic specially protected areas</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Antarctic specially protected areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Eleven terrestrial sites have been collectively designated as an <a href="/wiki/Antarctic_Specially_Protected_Area" title="Antarctic Specially Protected Area">Antarctic specially protected area</a> (ASPA&#160;140), primarily for their botanic and ecological values, because the island has the greatest number of rare plant species of any place in the Antarctic. This is largely due to frequent volcanic activity creating new substrates for plant colonisation:<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Collins_Point" title="Collins Point">Collins Point</a> (site&#160;A) contains good examples of long-established vegetation, with high species diversity and several rarities.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Crater_Lake_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="Crater Lake (South Shetland Islands)">Crater Lake</a> (site&#160;B) has a <a href="/wiki/Scoria" title="Scoria">scoria</a>-covered <a href="/wiki/Lava" title="Lava">lava tongue</a> with a diverse <a href="/wiki/Cryptogam" title="Cryptogam">cryptogamic</a> flora, and exceptional development of <a href="/wiki/Sod" title="Sod">turf</a>-forming <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a>.</li>
<li>An unnamed hill at the southern end of Fumarole Bay (site&#160;C) has several rare species of mosses that have colonised the heated soil crust close to a line of volcanic vents.</li>
<li>Fumarole Bay (site&#160;D) is <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geologically</a> complex with the most diverse flora on the island.</li>
<li>West <a href="/wiki/Stonethrow_Ridge" title="Stonethrow Ridge">Stonethrow Ridge</a> (site&#160;E) supports several rare mosses, <a href="/wiki/Liverwort" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverwort">liverworts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichens</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Telefon_Bay" title="Telefon Bay">Telefon Bay</a> (site&#160;F) has all its surfaces dating from 1967, thus allowing accurate monitoring of colonisation by plants and animals.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pendulum_Cove" title="Pendulum Cove">Pendulum Cove</a> (site&#160;G) is another known-age site being colonised by mosses and lichens.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mount_Pond" title="Mount Pond">Mount Pond</a> (site&#160;H) contains exceptional moss, liverwort, and lichen <a href="/wiki/Plant_community" title="Plant community">communities</a>.</li>
<li>Perchue Cone (site&#160;J) is an <a href="/wiki/Cinder_cone" title="Cinder cone">ash and cinder cone</a> with rare mosses.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Hill_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="Ronald Hill (South Shetland Islands)">Ronald Hill</a> to <a href="/wiki/Kroner_Lake" title="Kroner Lake">Kroner Lake</a> (site&#160;K) is another known-age site being colonised by numerous cryptogam species, and with a unique <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algal</a> community on the lake shore.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/South_East_Point_(South_Shetland_Islands)" title="South East Point (South Shetland Islands)">South East Point</a> (site&#160;L) supports the most extensive population of <a href="/wiki/Colobanthus_quitensis" title="Colobanthus quitensis">Antarctic pearlwort</a> known in the Antarctic region.</li></ul>
<p>In addition, two marine sites in <a href="/wiki/Port_Foster" title="Port Foster">Port Foster</a> have collectively been designated ASPA&#160;145, to protect their <a href="/wiki/Benthos" title="Benthos">benthic</a> communities.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Important_bird_area">Important bird area</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Deception_Island&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Important bird area"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Baily_Head" title="Baily Head">Baily Head</a>, a prominent headland forming the easternmost extremity of the island, has been identified as an <a href="/wiki/Important_Bird_Area" title="Important Bird Area">important bird area</a> (IBA) by <a href="/wiki/BirdLife_International" title="BirdLife International">BirdLife International</a> because it supports a very large <a href="/wiki/Bird_colony" title="Bird colony">breeding colony</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chinstrap_penguin" title="Chinstrap penguin">chinstrap penguins</a> (100,000&#160;pairs). The 78&#160;ha (190-acre) IBA comprises the ice-free headland and about 800 metres (0.50&#160;mi) of beach on either side of it. Other birds known to nest at the site include <a href="/wiki/Brown_skua" title="Brown skua">brown skuas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_petrel" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape petrel">Cape petrels</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Snowy_sheathbill" title="Snowy sheathbill">snowy sheathbills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bli_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bli-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
